I have the food stains in my copy of the book to prove it inspired me enough to try some new things out.<br /><br />Organization:  I've read reviews complaining about the organization or lack thereof.  True, the book does jump around, but the introduction is very clear about the layout of the book, it is supposed to be a reference book and not necessarily meant to be read sequentially.  I skipped a number of sections, scanned over others, intently read or re-read other sections and dog eared pages I will definitely return to (sorry Tim).<br /><br />Takeaway:  I learned new skills, was inspired to try some new techniques and plan to revisit a number of areas in the book repeatedly.  Felt it was and is well worth the money as it will continue to get use after making the first run through its pages.

I've uninstalled the app completely (though I wouldn't even be surprised to find that it left some \\"remnant\\" behind that is going to RE-install itself somehow!) NO app should be \\"unkillable\\".  Ever.  Not when I'm doing it through internal \\"force closes\\" at the Services level!<br /><br />I've installed the Watchdog app to make sure that avast! (or any other app) will not do this in the future.  If you have any concerns about losing control of your Android system, I would NOT recommend installing the avast! B009AMANBA|5.0|Steven Spielberg and Tony Kushner made some interesting and difficult choices in Lincoln that I think have succeeded in making a brilliant film about one of the most written about historical figures ever, and certainly the most written about and familiar American historical figure.  And yet despite a billion words written about this man he still somehow remains an enigma with something withheld and unrevealable about the man.  No doubt that is his continuing fascination to us and I have no doubt many more millions of words will be written, again vainly trying to get at the essence of the man.  It is far easier to gaze in wonderous respect at the marble statue in his unmatched Memorial than to try to find the human being within the marble.<br /><br />Spielberg and Kushner have done their best to try to find the man with the inestimable assistance of Daniel Day Lewis' genius.  If they haven't succeeded completely, well they are in good company with a thousand other biographers.  I liked the closeness and intimacy of the film.  I liked the quiet.  I liked the touching, beautiful and subtle small details: Lincoln lying down on the floor next to his sleeping son, the ever present shawl on his shoulders, the often stooped gait, Lincoln's ready reach for the illustrative yet sometimes illusive joke or story told with great good humor, Lincoln holding hands with Stimson as the war news comes in, Lincoln's fondness for and engagement with his young aides and soldiers, his gentle touches and the incredible mastery of his emotions, his rectitude and subtle manipulation of the obstreperous, passionate, often obtuse political allies and foes.<br /><br />Throughout, Day Lewis is masterful in his delivery, conveying the homeliness of the man and yet the incredible strength and the sorrow that was with him every day of his Presidency that brought many of his detractors, especially Seward and others in the \\"team of rivals\\" to come to respect and love him.  He's got not just the look, the voice, the walk and movements of the man down, he has the gentleness, and the innate dignity of the man as well. This is Lincoln at the end of the war and his soul-aching weariness coupled with his steely resolution is evident in every frame.  He's superb.  The rest of the characters in the drama have been cast carefully with wonderful actors who actually often resemble the real men they're playing.  I could single out Tommy Lee Jones, David Straithairn, James Spader etc., but frankly everyone is marvelous in this cast down to every one of the maddening and quarrelsome Congressmen.<br /><br />And I thought Sally Fields was a fine Mary Lincoln.  Their scenes together played very well and conveyed in a few brief lines the struggles, regrets, tragic losses and difficulties that divide and also unite a long married couple who have weathered many travails.  I found it convincing.<br /><br />And finally, I am glad the focus of the film was the struggle to pass the 13th Amendment.  Unless you're a history buff, I imagine this will come as some surprise to many and I found their handling of the politics and personalities at play both fascinating and engaging.  I was absorbed and I imagine others will find revelatory the difficulty of passing this crucial legislation. And why not focus on this often overlooked struggle?  As the film carefully explains, the whole moral purpose of the war, abolition, could have been undone postwar without it.<br /><br />Some may find this narrowing of the events of the film to the last 6 months of Lincoln's life and the struggle to legislate a disappointment.  Not me.  As mentioned, we have had millions of words and many films and documentaries covering the overview of Lincoln's life. I applaud Spielberg and Kushner making an intimate film closeup and intense and, yes, full of dialogue and argument as the framework to illustrate an exceptional man in unimaginably difficult and tragic times, and finding within this closeup a glimpse of the man and his relations with wife, children, and friends and foes.  It is a brilliantly acted and directed illustration of democracy being tested to its limits, ornery and contentious even within the midst of Civil War, and human beings at their most venal and at their most noble.<br /><br />Many insights and much of this history is conveyed in dialogue (Lincoln's admission of his assumption of powers not necessarily granted him and ignoring of the law when he deemed it necessary is a prime example) and a potent line here and there speaks volumes about the war, the law, the Presidency, his marriage, his sorrow, his guile, and his steadfastness.  Nicely done and will promote repeated viewing.<br /><br />As expected from Spielberg, the production values are marvelous.  Well done in all departments.

0618918248|3.0|This review will be written from a certain Chrtistian perspective. However, I will make an effort to be fair minded and objective; which is more than I can say for much of The God Delusion. Richard Dawkins objective in writing this book, as stated at the beginning of the second paragraph on page 28 of the 2008 paper back edtion is,\\"If this book works as I intend, religious readers who open it will be atheists when they put it down.\\" If that is his goal then this book is an abysmal failure for it had quite the opposite effect on this reviewer; for after reading it I believe more strongly than ever that there is a God. I find it difficult to believe that I would be alone in this reaction.<br /><br />The God Delusion is an engagingly written even frequently entertaining book. Mr. Dawkins is obviously a fine writer and an excellent scientist. He does a wonderful job of stating the various principles of his own field, evolutionary biology, and related areas in terms which are very accessable to the layman and novice. As a result there much to be learned about the thinking behind evolution, some of which is in fact valid and corresponds to some degree with the reality of how life developed and diversified on this earth. It is the conclusion of Richard Dawkins and others that there is no room and no need for God as creator that is in error. Meme's are his artificial constructs which which function as the sociological counterpart to gene's in biology. He uses them to quantify and catagorize behavior systems in sentient species. He would reduce belief in God to a misfriing of a mechanism originally developed through natural selection for another purpose.<br /><br />Richard Dawkins admits that there are two seemingly insurmountable obstacles to a godless totally naturalistic explantion for the development of the universe and the life therein which are: the development of life from lifelessness and the origins of consciousness and intelligence. It has been said that DNA the building block of all life is a complex chemical language or code with its corresponding order and syntax which are far from random. In the famous Miller experiment of the 50's and its more recent variations amino acids were created under laboratory conditions which are components of the proteins which make up DNA; but there have been no true life generating results. Continuing the language analogy the results of these experiments have been jibberish. If scientists ever do succeed in \\"creating life\\" it will result from the intelligence of minds somehow reordering the amino acids into their proper sequence maybe with the aid of computers. This would strongly suggest the need for a super intelligence ie God to have developed life in the first place.<br /><br />I'm not sure what Richard Dawkins belief's are that he is trying to explain in his attempt to dismantle Thomas Aquinas famous proofs for the existence of God. It is one of the most basic and unavoidable scientific truths that every effect  has a cause and the universe is an immensely large effect which demands an immensely powerful cause. There are two choices; either an infinite regress an endless chain of cause and effect which had no beginning and has no end or something or someone where the \\"buck stops.\\" It seems he would he prefer an infinite regress to the idea of God as the terminator to the regress, the uncaused source of everything; that if a terminator is even a valid concept it is something mindless.<br /><br />Mr. Dawkins mind seems so closed to the idea of God that he does not consider theology(the study of God) to be a legitimate field of knowledge worthy of an academic degree; he therefore dismisses out of hand any discussion of the possible nature of God as nonsense. His attitude toward the Bible is little better. Although he does consider the King James or Authorized version to be an important literary document and contribution to the english language, to him it is nothing more than a  collectionof myths or stories based in fabricated or extremely flawed history ie it is almost completely lacking in historicity. There are many books revealing research which give the lie to this position such as  \\" The Case For Christ\\" by Lee Strobel or \\"The Historical Jesus\\" by Gary R. Habermas. Don't accept liberal criticism of scripture at face value without your own research. It seems Mr. Dawkins has done little of his own Biblical research but quotes liberal scholars who make conclusions supporting his overall opinion. In the past such men claimed that the Old Testament people the Hittites never existed; however archeologists later confirmed their existence.<br /><br />Given this attitude toward scripture it is understandable why Richard Dawkins would not make extensive use of it in trying to plead his case for the non-existence of God and why he would make such obvious mistakes concerning what it says, mistakes that Sunday School children would not make. Richard Dawkins tries to create a conflict between the three gospels that mention Christ's Birth or detail events surrounding it. According to Luke, Jesus parents Mary and Joseph were living in Nazareth in Galilee and journeyed to Bethlehem in Judea for the tax census where Jesus was born, later returning to Nazareth. Matthew makes no mention of where they were living before but does state in Chapter two that He was born in Bethlehem. Dawkins argues based on the logical fallacy of what is not said that they were living in Bethlehem all along. Matthew states however that Mary, Joseph and Jesus came to live in Nazareth after the death of Herod, in no way suggesting the parents had never lived there before. In John people in the crowds following Jesus state their belief that Jesus was born in Nazareth; John however makes it clear a few verses later that he believed Jesus to have been born in Bethlehem by stating the fact that was where the prophets said the messiah was to be born. There is no conflict between the gospelson this issue simply a different perspective.<br /><br />Richard Dawkins claims that no one gets their moral values from the Bible. While the Bible is not the only source for such values it does contain important moral teaching such as; love mercy and justice, care for widows and orphans and when harvesting leave behind food for the poor. Jesus taught us to do unto others what you would want them to do to you, to love and pray for for your enemies, and to love your neighbor as yourself. Mr. Dawkins claims that Jesus was a racist and a Jewish exclusivist but the example He gives of who that neighboor might be was a Samaritan, one of the people most despised by the Jews. He also spoke to a Samaritan woman.Many women were among His followers and were the first witnesses to His resurrection. In a society where women were considered of little value Jesus elevated them to a position of priveledge. The many detestable acts recorded in the Bible are not there because it approves of them but to show what happens when people turn from God doing whatever \\"is right in their own eyes.\\"<br /><br />Richard Dawkins determined belief that God does not exist boils down to one thing; ignorant people do evil things in the name of God and  religion therefore religion is evil and there is no God.  He all but dismisses the idea that people who do such things are not following the teachings of Christ or of good religion; from the crusades and inquisitions of centuries past incited by the so-called church, or people today who murder abortion clinic doctors or the \\"American Taliban\\" who would turn the USA into a so called Christian theocracy. The millions of Christians who would not resort to violence he accuses of encouraging those who would when they point to certain evils in our world. He Says that he and any atheists he knows would not kill or destroy for their cause; but by insisting that religion is evil, by his own argument is he not encouraging atheists who do believe in violence. The greatest attrocities of the twentieth century have been committed by atheists such as Soviet dictator Joseph Stalin or Cambodia's Pol Pot.<br /><br />Alister Mcgrath author of \\"The Dawkins Delusion\\" who holds a doctorate in molecular biophysics and is now a leading theologian is well aacquainted with the views of leading scientists, both believers in God and atheists. He states that they do not derive their atheism from their science but bring their atheism to their science. Scientific evidence demands neither a belief in the existence or non-existence of God. The apparent division between science and religion that has existed for centuries is the product of closed minded indivduals on both sides who refuse to ask the right questions or accept the answers. The truth is of the people who will read \\"The God Deludion\\" most of those who want to believe in God will continue to do so, probably more strongly than ever, and most of those who want to believe there is no God will become atheists. Maybe Richard Dawkins could create meme's to explain the behavior of each.

0606262229|4.0|Maggie Stiefvater's tales of winter werewolves have always been far more striking and poetic than any other werewolf books I can think of. And she brings the story of Grace and Sam to a close in \\"Forever,\\" a hauntingly bittersweet, sumptuously-written coming-of-age tale with a somewhat flawed finale -- it's a bit too rushed and pat, but otherwise quite satisfying.<br /><br />Spring has returned Grace to her human form, but she's still unstable -- she keeps turning back into a wolf and running into the woods. Sam has spent the whole winter waiting for her, despite the people of Mercy Falls thinking he's a budding serial killer. And Cole is hotly pursuing a cure for lycanthropy, using himself as a guinea pig.<br /><br />However, Sam and Grace's idyllic reunion is ruined by another death -- another girl is found savaged by a wolf (pretty obviously Shelby). Isabel's father arranges for the wolves to be exterminated (with HELICOPTERS), leaving the teens only a few days to lead the wolves to safety. Otherwise, Grace may be among the dead.<br /><br />Maggie Stiefvater is one of the rare young-adult authors who has lyrical, hauntingly lovely writing. Fragmented thoughts arrange themselves into minimalist poems, and mundane situations take on the delicate crystalline quality of a romantic dream (\\"it was just me, broken into pieces, slivered like glass, made into something new\\").<br /><br />\\"Forever\\" centers on three important subplots -- the need to save the wolf pack from Isabel's revenge-obsessed father, the quest for a lycanthropy cure (especially for Cole), and the teenagers shedding their childhood problems as they prepare to set out into adulthood. The story drifts along between these three subplots, with some bloody, tightly-paced action scenes (like the grand finale) woven in.<br /><br />And her characters are just as brilliant as her writing -- four troubled teenagers, who are breaking away from their pasts and their weird parents. Grace and Sam settle into an idyllic little world of their own, but are haunted by the hostility towards Sam and Grace's feelings about her parents. And Stiefvater spends a lot of time focusing on Cole and Isabel's tumultuous relationship, as Cole goes all brilliant mad scientist.<br /><br />One problem: the ending is rushed. Isabel, Cole and Grace take dramatic actions that seem like they should have massive consequences... but they don't. At all. Shouldn't Isabel's dad be having a rage-induced stroke or something?<br /><br />The payoff feels rushed and a little incomplete, but otherwise \\"Forever\\" is a striking, romantic little finale for Stiefvater's brilliant trilogy. This is everything \\"Twilight\\" failed to be.unted by the hostility towards Sam and Grace's feelings about her parents. So how does THE EXPENDABLES 2 stack up?<br /><br />The opening sequence offers up the action quota quite well and we get to see the team in action. We also meet a new member, a sniper by the name of Bill (Liam Hemsworth). Each member is given enough screen time to earn them their paycheck and before the sequence ends, team member Yin (Jet Li) parachutes out of their plane never to return for the rest of the film.<br /><br />When they return home ready for some R & R, Barney (Sylvester Stallone) is contacted by Church (Bruce Willis). Unhappy with the outcome from the first film, he tells Barney he has another mission for the team, an easy one that will square things away between them. Mission in hand and the addition of a CIA operative Church sends along, the group sets out for a small European country to retrieve some codes locked in a safe.<br /><br />The group retrieves the codes and is ready to head out when they're confronted by a problem they weren't warned about. Vilain (Jean-Claude Van Damme) and his men have the team surrounded and Bill with a gun to his head. The team can do nothing but give in and surrender the codes. Even though they've complied, Vilain kills Bill in front of them before leaving. Of course this sets the revenge ball rolling and Barney will stop at nothing until he gets the codes back and sees Vilain dead.<br /><br />The premise for the film is rather simple but that's never been a problem with either film. It's a core story that surrounds itself with tons of action and special effects. That's what these films are all about. That and half a dozen hand to hand combat sequences that would result in work for half the stunt men in the world. These films are action films made for fans and for fun. And the new one delivers, for the most part.<br /><br />This time around though it feels different. For one the surprise has been taken out of the equation. The first film we all wondered what it would be like to see some of the biggest names in action films from the 80s together on the screen at the same time. We got that and this time around we get it in spades. We have the members of the original cast together again and Willis and Schwarzenegger are even allowed to play with the rest this time around. Not only that, but Van Damme and Chuck Norris are tossed in as well. Norris has an especially funny part in the film. And yet it doesn't feel the same.<br /><br />Perhaps it's seeing all of our heroes from the past aging just a bit before our eyes even though every one of them still seems fit and perhaps more so than when they were the hottest thing in action films. Maybe it's that the quips and witty one liners we've come to associate with them feel rather old hat here. Yes, they are cute but for me they came up too often. I'm not sure what it is but it made me feel that this film wasn't quite as good as the first one.<br /><br />That being said it's still a great action film. And seeing Willis, Schwarzenegger and Stallone shooting their way through an airport, all of them in the same shot, was amazing. This is not an action film where you'll find yourself wondering how plausible the movie is or if the situations seen could really happen. This movie is a roller coaster ride that takes you up and down, tosses you around and then makes you want to go for another ride. It's a popcorn movie, plain and simple, and one to be enjoyed for just that reason.<br /><br />Word is that a third film is in the works. It will be interesting to see what other action stars of the 80s are brought back for this one. Steve Seagal? Mel Gibson? Perhaps they'll choose a different route and bring in action stars of today with the hopes of making this series of films last longer with a new crew taking on bad guys. No one knows except Stallone who's been behind both films. Let's just hope it continues and only gets better with each film.oose a different route and bring in action stars of today with the hopes of making this series of films last longer with a new crew taking on bad guys. No one knows except Stallone who's been behind both films. Let's just hope it continues and only gets better with each film.

B009369Z8A|4.0|It's been years since the theme of bootleggers was the subject matter in movies. Back in the 70s there was a rush of movies about this subject ranging from the low budget MOONRUNNERS (the movie later turned into the hit TV series THE DUKES OF HAZARD) to the even lower budgeted MOONSHINERS. Even Burt Reynolds took on the subject in WHITE LIGHTNING. But then it kind of disappeared. That all changed when reality TV took a shine (pun intended) to the topic and the film LAWLESS is a result of that renewed interest.<br /><br />Based loosely on the real life story of the three Bondurant brothers in Franklin County, Virginia, the story focuses on a short period of their lives when bootlegging was their claim to fame and the end result was what was called a war in their home county. Descendants of the real life family have written a book on the subject and that is what the film is based on.<br /><br />The Bondurant brothers were legends in Franklin County. Oldest brother Forrest (Tom Hardy) was said to be indestructible having crossed paths with death on several occasions. Middle brother Howard (Jason Clarke) has perhaps decided to dip into the family recipe too often but remains the muscle of the group. The youngest brother, Jack (Shia LeBouf) is the upstart, trying to think of ways to impress his older brother Forrest and increase the profits of their bootlegging venture. But Forrest is content to sit back and make the money that he does from their product and pay his bribe money to the local sheriff.<br /><br />All that changes when a new prosecutor comes to town. Charlie Rakes (Guy Pearce) is part of a task force that was sent to shut down the stills but who in truth is more interested in taking over the entire county's bootlegging business. When Forrest refuses to comply, Rakes sets out to destroy the Bondurant family in any way possible. The result is a violent and bloody confrontation that leaves Forrest wounded but alive and his brothers ready for revenge. But that is not to happen yet.<br /><br />Jack decides the best way to increase their finances is to begin selling their product to Chicago gangster Floyd Banner (Gary Oldman). With the country dry due to prohibition, Jack can get good money from the mobster in return for supplying the demand the gangsters need for their town. While the brothers may disagree on this item the money does come in handy at the right time.<br /><br />Rakes' men having been behind the attack on Forrest and the brutalization of a waitress and love interest of Forrest (Jessica Chastain) that same night have left a bad taste in the mouths of the brothers. When they blow up their still and murder Jack's best friend in cold blood, a harmless young boy who had no chance of being a problem to Rakes, the brothers can take no more. An eventual showdown between the corrupt lawman and the bootleggers is inevitable. It's bloody but not overly so and the results are surprising.<br /><br />LAWLESS does a great job of capturing the era and area that the film takes place in. The back hills of Virginia look beautiful rather than wasted away and yet the people who live there looks as poor as the times the story takes place in. While bootlegging may have paid the bills for poor farmers who made more money this way it was not the glamorous life that say cocaine dealers have been depicted in more modern stories. These were tough men who did what they had to to feed their families and keep their farms. The work was hard and the rewards merely enough to get by. There was no glitz and glamour here.<br /><br />The acting here is stupendous. Tom Hardy turns in another dynamite performance as a man who uses few words and fewer actions yet carries the threat of violence about him like an aura. His character knows the ways of the world and tries to convey them with little success to his younger brother. LeBouf does a great job as well, depicting a hero worshipping brother who wants to do well by his family yet gets turned downmore often than not. Pearce is equal to these two in depicting a bad guy that even law abiding citizens will find themselves hoping gets his due.<br /><br />The movie doesn't offer a pretty picture of the bootlegging business but it does offer a few new anti-heroes for viewers to root for. You care about this family and the others who faced these problems in the past. It was a violent world that handled things much differently than they are handled today. And that makes for some tremendous storytelling that just might make viewers want to find out more and read about those times.more often than not. Pearce is equal to these two in depicting a bad guy that even law abiding citizens will find themselves hoping gets his due.<br /><br />The movie doesn't offer a pretty picture of the bootlegging business but it does offer a few new anti-heroes for viewers to root for. B004XGN8W4|3.0|I wanted a way to easily transport my Xbox 360 to a friend's house (or anywhere else that makes sense).  This allows that, plus it has a built-in ~15\\" screen to play on.  Perfect, right?  Mostly.<br /><br />Yes, it transports my Xbox console along with its power \\"brick\\" and other necessary accessories.  And yes, the built-in screen is JUST good enough to be acceptable for console gaming (the screen could use a better viewing angle and better color/contrast overall).  But the gaming case can only really store one controller in the case, because the rest of the space goes to other wires needed for this case to do its job.  There's an HDMI cable (from the Xbox to the screen), and a power adapter and wire for the screen.  Here's where the shortcomings begin...<br /><br />Too many wires without an effective wire management system inside the case.  If I have to power two devices (video game console and screen), I would expect that the wiring for these devices is neatly organized inside the case for quick and easy gaming on the go.  I want to open the case, plug the whole thing in (ONE POWER PLUG IN THE WALL PLEASE!), take out my controller, hit power, and play.  Instead, I have take all of the wires and adapter out, plug them all in to the devices inside the case, maneuver those wires a bit, plug TWO power adapter into the wall (or power strip).  Couldn't it have been everything all ready to go inside the case, and just run one power cable into the wall?  That would have made A LOT more sense.  Of course, this wiring/setup issue really only adds a minute or two to the process... but it's just not very convenient, and I think it could have been done better.  BUT IT ALL WORKS despite my complaint about wiring (don't hate me for hating), and this is my only real complaint.  So moving on...<br /><br />Last complaint (a little one)... is that the case doesn't offer much protection to the devices inside.  I know that the makers of this \\"mobile system\\" do not claim it protects well, so it's not false advertising.  But certainly, if I have these relatively fragile electronic devices in a cool-looking mobile carry case... my expectation is that they're decently protected.  I don't think they are, honestly.  For JUST carrying?  Sure.  And once it's placed down, set up, and being used... no problem.  But on the go... my concern is one good drop or similar incident -- and something is not going to work when you hit power next time.<br /><br />I'll end with this: I really like this thing.  I only focused on the complaints because in reality -- this thing is pretty much what it needs to be.  I can pretty easily lug my big Xbox over to a friend's place and play beside him without transporting TV's around his house?  AWESOME.  And look cool in the process?  (From a gamer's view, anyway...)  Very nice.  I'm excited to have this thing, especially since the idea for something like this has been in every gamers' head since they first grabbed a video game controller.  I would like to see improvements in the next iteration of this thing (and I believe there may actually be a newer one - or two - as I write this).  But for what it is, and what I paid... I have no regrets about my purchase.<br /><br />You a gamer?  Know one?  Dream of moving about the world with your console-of-choice in tow?  This is it.  This is the thing you need.

1400052181|5.0|I add my voice to the many kudos and awards \\"Immortal Life\\" has won since its publication. There are multiple fascinating stories within this book, that of Henrietta Lacks herself, of how her cells have advanced medical research and of the long saga of her family to fully understand Henrietta's life and the impact of her contribution to science. It's also the story of medical and pharmaceutical industries profiting from Henrietta's cells while being oblivious to the concerns of her family and only belatedly recognizing her contribution. The author does not belabor this point, but the book inherently critiques America's health care system. Despite their matriarch's incredible contribution to the welfare of millions, the Lackses are a poor family who have no insurance to help them with their own illnesses.<br /><br />I have enormous respect for Rebecca's Skloot's persistence in investigating the story of Henrietta Lacks and her descendants. She spent years earning their trust, unraveling their story and presenting it to us in this can't-wait-to-turn-the-page book. I'm kind of a science idiot, and I thought that aspect of the book might lose me. But the science never gets too complex, and what there is she explains very simply and clearly so that most readers should have no problem grasping it. It's much more than a science book anyway.<br /><br />\\"Immortal Life of Henrietta Lacks\\" is the inter-generational story of an American family, the impact of racism and poverty on their lives, and their quest for truth and understanding. The chapter in which Henrietta's daughter and son were finally able to view their mother's live cells projected on a screen in a lab was tear-inducing for this reader. What an extraordinary, true story! This book is an instant American classic.

0375507256|5.0|I loved Cloud Atlas, though it definitely takes some getting into, and I didn't love it at first. It is a fascinating story, spanning over six time periods: the 19th century, the 1930s, the 1970s, the present day, a near-future Big Brother type society in Korea, post-apocalyptic Hawaii, and then back again. David Mitchell is a really amazing writer. This one is so different from Black Swan Green, yet equally well done, and certainly more complex. I really enjoyed all of the stories here, with possibly the exception of the first and last story, the one in the 19th century. The writing was a bit off-putting there, though the second half of it was good. David Mitchell shifts almost effortlessly from historical fiction to science fiction.<br /><br />The next obvious question is: are the stories interconnected? And yes, they are. In each one, some mention is made of either a person or a book or a piece of music in the previous story. And there are some more subtle references as well, like the comet-shaped birthmark that many of the characters share. As you may know, a movie just came out of Cloud Atlas. I may watch it, though I doubt it's as good as the book.<br /><br />This one has really great characters. I especially liked Luisa Rey, the smart and sharp journalist from the 1970s. She's determined to uncover the truth, no matter the consequences, and I really admired that about her. Sonmi-451 is not bad either, and very smart.<br /><br />I liked the way that Mitchell structured the book too. Each of the first sections of the stories ends on a cliffhanger: either the sentence cuts off in the middle or something momentous happens, and you just have to wait until it comes back around again (though of course, you could cheat and skip ahead, if only to see whether the character survives).<br /><br />I would highly recommend this one, but if you find the first section a little boring, stick with it. The rest are much better.<br /><br />My blog is located at novareviews.blogspot.com (Cleo's Literary Reviews).

In its place lies utter garbage.<br /><br />The pop songs were bad enough, but this... THIS?!?!?  Whatever Mike Oldfield was going for here is completely unacceptable.  \\"Nothing But\\" shows that Oldfield was interested in mainstream soul that the likes of Whitney Houston and several others brought into the picture.  While not a bad type of music by itself, ask yourself this- does it REALLY belong on a Mike Oldfield album?  Absolutely not.  \\"Bridge to Paradise\\" has the same generic guitar work that Kenny Loggins used on \\"Danger Zone\\" and the vocals even resemble Kenny Loggins quite a bit.  For some reason though, I don't *completely* hate this song. It's caught somewhere in between commercial spirituality and pop music.  For me it doesn't work very well, but at least the vocals sound honest enough.  The chorus is obviously trying to mimmick the early 70's Moody Blues because it sounds like a severely watered down version of \\"Isn't Life Strange?\\"  Still, I actually like the song.  Perhaps there is a legitimate attempt at putting Oldfield's vision in a different light here, but my gut feeling tells me that it's probably all a big put-on and just an attempt at going commercial which means we can't take it as seriously as Oldfield's golden year period (1973-1981).  AdrianBelew does a nice job singing the melody at any rate.  A far cry from his King Crimson days of course.  I keep thinking \\"Far Country\\" is actually \\"Far Cry\\" (which is fitting, really). I have a lot of trouble even sitting through it, in fact.<br /><br />\\"Hostage\\" makes the fatal mistake of including horns and heavy guitars at the same time.  Not a big deal any other time.  I mean Genesis used to combine the two really well and those songs are terrific.  So what's the problem here?  The songwriting is mid-tempo boredom and the lead singer sounds identical to Noddy Holder, the lead singer of Slade minus the soaring range.  \\"Runaway Son\\" sounds like the theme song to some horribly dated family-oriented show from the mid 80's.<br /><br />NOW do people understand why I'm so hard on the 80's?  This is why originality is important- without it, everything turns bland and sounds the same.  I honestly feel nauseous right now.  This is just awful, awful awful.  HIGHLY recommended that you skip this.  This isn't even Mike Oldfield.

B000002UAC|5.0|By the time this album was released in the UK (its release date, November 22nd 1963, happened to coincide with JFK's assassination), Beatlemania was in full swing in Britain. The band had already had 4 hit singles, 2 (or 3, depending on which chart you use) of which had gone to #1 and were shortly to be followed by 'I Want To Hold Your Hand'. 'She Loves You' had been in the charts for 3 months and had recently gone back up to #1. The first album, 'Please Please Me', had been the #1 album for 29 weeks and only another Beatles album was going to knock it off the top. If ever an album was set up for the sophomore jinx to strike, this was it. There was no way for The Beatles to meet the expectations their career thus far had created.<br /><br />This background is important, because 'With The Beatles' is one of the most overlooked Beatles albums. Its anonymity is further enhanced by the imminent breakthrough of the band in America. 'With The Beatles' was reshaped in the US and retitled 'Meet The Beatles' and millions of American fans still remember that as the first and most exciting Beatles album they ever heard- rightly, because MTB is a great album.<br /><br />However, 'With The Beatles', now the definitive second album in the Beatles CD canon, really does hold up extraordinarily well. It follows the formula of the first album in offering 8 originals and 6 covers. The covers chosen for this album are very strong, with three out-and-out rockers ('Please Mr. Postman', 'Roll Over Beethoven' and 'Money'), the ballad 'Til There Was You' and a powerful rendition of the Smokey Robinson song 'You Really Got A Hold On Me'. Only 'Devil In Her Heart' sounds like it was put in to make up the numbers.<br /><br />The originals aren't quite as strong by The Beatles' own standards. 'It Won't Be Long' is a powerful opener and Ringo delivers a rousing version of 'I Wanna Be Your Man'. Paul's catchy 'All My Loving' was deemed strong enough to be the opening song on the band's first Ed Sullivan show and George's songwriting debut 'Don't Bother Me' is noteworthy for introducing a different lyrical idea from the usual boy/girl relationship songs. However, the remaining four songs, 'All I've Got To Do', 'Little Child', 'Hold Me Tight' and 'Not A Second Time' are mid-tempo songs with less to make them memorable. Don't get me wrong, they are good songs which any other group of the time would love to have written and recorded. It's just that The Beatles had already set the bar so high that these songs fall a little short of their best work.<br /><br />Overall, the album is the hardest-rocking of all the band's albums. The Beatles are tighter musically than in their debut (no doubt because they were given more than one day to record this one!) and the album has a more professional feel. It doesn't have quite the variety of 'Please Please Me' or the raw, fresh sound of that record. Nevertheless, it's a worthy follow-up, as the inclusion of 9 of the tracks on 'Meet The Beatles' makes clear.<br /><br />The Beatles had overcome the fear that they couldn't back up their early success, and were on their way to becoming legends. Next stop America!

B004Y8075M|5.0|Louis Lowry's The Giver is an award-winning Young Adult fictional novel found on the shelves of many Language Arts teachers and libraries. Many have summarized it as a coming of age book that is about a 12-year-old boy, Jonas, who lives in a perfect society. Lowry writes on the back cover, \\"Everything is under control. There is no war or fear or pain. There are no choices. Every person is assigned a role in the Community\\".<br /><br />When Jonas receives his life assignment to be the Receiver of Memories, he discovers secrets about the past, and the terrible choices that make this world possible. The previous Receiver, now called the Giver, trains him.<br /><br />The author continues, \\"The Giver alone holds the memories of the true pain and pleasure of life. Now it's time for Jonas to receive the truth.\\" Gradually Jonas comes to understand, and resent, the choices that had to be made to create his world, and the terrible secrets behind its perfection. Together he and the Giver concoct a plan to change the way his world works, but before they can carry it out Jonas is forced to make a decision that may destroy them all.<br /><br />For me as a student teacher and a parent of five adolescents/young adults, I found The Giver:<br /><br />* To be thought- and conversation provoking. I found the best part of reading The Giver is the many conversations it inspires -- from life and death, love and pain, and more.<br /><br />* To be anything but controlling for the reader. For a novel that is about control, I loved how Lowry left Jonas and Gabriel's fate up to the interpretation of the reader. The last moments of the novel were told in such as way that it allowed the reader wonder if Jonas and Gabriel's lives had ended (or released).<br /><br />* To be disturbing at times. I am concerned about age-inappropriate content for middle school students, including occultist themes and violence, sexually explicit material and the ideas of drug use, suicide and euthanasia. I found several passages unsettling:<br /><br />* Jonas' father punctures a newborn in the top of the forehead with a syringe full of lethal fluid. He talks to the crying baby, gently saying he knows it hurts. Then he nonchalantly wraps up the dead child and puts him in a trash bin.<br /><br />* Jonas and other young volunteers bathe the elderly in the House of the Old. People are forbidden to look at others naked, but this rule doesn't apply with infants or the elderly.<br /><br />* When Rosemary, the failed Receiver of Memory before Jonas, seeks release, she asks to inject the needle into herself.<br />While it may be commonplace for images as such to be on television and in the movies, I would want to make sure my students had plenty of opportunities to discuss, write, and or illustrate their thoughts and feelings.<br /><br />For me, the positives far outweigh the negatives of reading The Giver. This classic is a must read for all students who seek to broaden their understanding of life.

0547884591|5.0|As Hegel said, \\"Education is the art of making man ethical.\\" Now, you may be asking yourself and me, \\"Dude, why are you beginning your review with a Hegel quote, or a quote from anyone for that matter? Are you that pretentious: are you really 'that guy'?\\"<br />Firstly, quotes, whether taken out of context or not, give credence to the rhetorician wielding them; and, secondly, I've just shown two things that make Tim Ferriss and his newest book \\"The 4-Hour Chef\\" a must read. Let me explain.<br /><br />Have you ever read a book that claims it will teach you something only to open a book of quotes that have been robbed of their context to make you think you're learning something about the world and yourself? I know I have, and you have too. There is a difference between telling quotes to the reading and showing quotes, which is what, I argue, Ferriss does: he doesn't just provide an abstract quote \\"a good life is best lived when one provides themselves an understanding of x, y, z, \\"-(insert name of seemingly \\"enlightened\\" person), for Ferriss shows the reader how to live life more fully by telling stories and giving concrete examples.<br /><br />So, you want to learn a second, third, seventh, or, if you haven't already mastered someway of intuiting new languages just by smelling them a mile away, twenty-fifth language, Ferriss tells you how he did and continues to do it; to get a quick and powerful understanding of a language, he Deconstructs (like Bartelby the Scrivener, I would have \\"preferred not\\" to see the term Deconstruct(ion) used outside of the realm of Continental Philosophy) languages down into the 100 most used words, modal-auxiliaries (can, could, would, should, would like, etc.), and he asks native speakers, breaking all the rules with this one ya'll, for help. A really interesting story Ferriss provides is of Cardinal Giuseppi Mezofonti, who had a command of 39 languages and was, apparently, tested for fluency in up to 79 languages. Shit. In any case, Mezofonti's big secret, Ferriss says, is that when coming into contact with a new language he would ask a native speaker to write out the Lord's Prayer, which houses many of the structures of grammar and syntax needed to understand a language. All in all, Ferriss learned from his example and, upon meeting a new language, asks the native speaker 12 questions, the \\"Deconstruction Dozen,\\" that will help Ferriss intuit the rules that govern the new language's language-game.<br /><br />The above paragraph is the first of four big sections of the book dealing with Meta-Learning, or the Learning of Learning. If you thought Ferriss' friend Deconstruction, the section I explicated above, was a powerful tool for understanding then wait until you meet the other three friends making up the acronym DiSSS (Deconstruction, Selection, Sequencing, Stakes). Ferriss also provides the reader with the acronym CaFE (Compression, Frequency, and Encoding). All in all, these systems are a summation of every method, technique, habit, practice, you name it, for how to more easily understand, fully intuit, and pragmatically apply information.<br /><br />Here are three pros and cons, to display that this review is at least prima facie unbiased:<br /><br />Cons:<br />1) Could be more depth into memorization methods such as the Loci method. Although a seemingly very mysterious system, wherein one memorizes, let's say, a speech by placing pieces of it along a mentally constructed pathway, I am confident Ferriss could have provided an effective nutshell summation and example.<br /><br />2) The use of the word deconstruction is rampant throughout our context in history, and it is not being used appropriately in the context of its creator Derrida, so another word would have been nice.<br /><br />3) The meta-learning theory at the beginning could have been more explicitly applied throughout the rest of the book. DiSSS and CaFE model well to the understanding of creating amazing food, but applying it to everything and anything else is uncomfortable for those unsure of what they're doing; re-showing the methods in different contexts give the reader experience and practice so that they can apply it to piano or guitar or skiing or showering.<br /><br />Pros:<br />1) Section on language acquisition is out of this world. Even the brief story of Cardinal Mezofonti was a world shatterer. Thanks.<br /><br />2) I finally know how to make mayo from scratch that is firm. Amazing.<br /><br />3) My father is a veteran trained chef, who graduated top of his class at the prestigious Western Culinary Institute in the late 1980s, and this book scared the shit out of him. He's conservative, like Malcolm Gladwell, and told me that Ferriss theory simply couldn't produce any sort of good food in that short amount of time. We went through Ferriss' tips, tricks, and a few recipes together, and my father was surely impressed. He's coming around.<br /><br />So, thank you Tim Ferriss for the book.<br />To all of you who haven't read it yet, please do; it will change you in weird, wacky, and amazing ways; you'll be exactly who you've always wanted to be, but better. I promise.<br /><br />Live your history, love how you're living, and always focus and do what you love to be focusing on doing. This book is one of those books that will provide you the skills to get you ninety-nine percent of the way to your goals; however, remember, you have to do the impossible: you have to believe in yourself and leap the last one percent.<br /><br />Happy Thursday and Stay excellent,<br />Arlo Tobin

1400052181|5.0|When the author took a community college biology class in 1988, her professor was explaining cancer cells and he wrote the name Henrietta Lacks on the board. He explained that Henrietta died in 1951 of cervical cancer. But, before she died, a surgeon took samples of her tumor and put them in a petri dish. The professor then added on that Henrietta was a black woman. Rebecca became intrigued about who the woman was behind the cells. She spent the next several years researching the story of the cells and that of Henrietta and her family.<br />Henrietta was born in Roanoke, Virginia in 1920. When her mother died, she returned to her father's family tobacco farm in Clover, VA. The family had farmed the same land since their slave ancestors. She grew up with her older cousin David, Day, Lacks. He was 5 years older. At age 14, Henrietta became pregnant with Day's child and they married. They had 5 children. Day was always cheating on Henrietta and gave her various STD'S.<br /><br />In 1951, after waiting a year, Henrietta went to John Hopkins Hospital to see a Doctor. She told them she had a knot in her womb. As the Dr. flipped through her chart from previous visits, he noted she had been diagnosed with neurosyphilis but had cancelled treatments. She had also tested positive for gonorrhea and increased cellular activity in the cervix. She had declined follow up treatment. Shortly after, Henrietta had given birth to a baby at the hospital yet, no tumor was detected at time of birth. Either it had been overlooked or it had grown that fast after 4 months. A sample of the tumor was taken and sent to pathology. When the Dr. began treatment on the tumor, he took samples of healthy tissue and the cancerous tissue. He then sent them to Dr. George Gey's lab. Gey was experimenting in growing cells from tissue. So far he was not having success in keeping cells alive. Henrietta's cells were different. They grew. He labeled his samples with the first two letters of the patient's firstand last name. These cells are now known as HeLa cells.<br /><br />HeLa cells with their unique properties became the cells to test every vaccine or procedure on. They were used to test the Salk vaccine for polio, radiation from a nuclear bomb, chemotherapy drugs, hormones, AIDS, deep sea diving and spaceflight. They were also infected with TB, salmonella and bacteria. It was later discovered that her cancer was caused by the HPV virus. HeLa cells became a researcher's dream. Factories were built to mass produce the cells. They were shipped all over the world, first freely by Dr. Gey, then for money by companies.<br />It wasn't until a Rolling Stone reporter showed up at the Lack's home in 1975, did the family find out that Henrietta's cells were still alive and being used for research. This had quite an effect on the family.<br /><br />Now in the 1990's, Ms. Skloot goes back to the Rolling Stone article and follows the research into the Lack's family. It takes time and patience but through numerous interviews and gaining confidence with the Lack's family, they let her in. Through a timeline back and forth, which aids in keeping track of where the author is in the book, we learn the science of the cells, the family relations of Henrietta, the ethical questions it raises about using cells from a donor or in many cases, not a donor, and making money from them. Henrietta's family never saw a cent from the millions the cells have made for companies. They have lived in poverty with no health insurance. I believe the book is very fair in showing both sides. Without testing on tissues, organs, blood, etc. after we are done with them, either in surgery or through lab work, there would be no way to find new cures for diseases. Yet, here is a family who could have really needed some compensation. Maybe John Hopkins could have at the very least provided free health care to the family as a sigh of good will. That is just my opinion. In the past couple of years, new laws have been written to protect the privacy and rights of the patients. We are a more informed patient.

Love the song, and whatever the \\"body electric\\" is, I'm singing it as I write this.<br /><br />\\"Bel Air\\" is just kind of there, but in all fairness, rather than give it a chance I always start the CD over when it comes on to get back to \\"Ride\\", the first single and arguably the best song on the EP. B004ZCUFPY|4.0|Fast Five adds an interesting twist to the Fast & Furious franchise, leaning more towards heist flick than a street racing film. Universal Studios has breathed new life into the series by switching up the formula, and Fast Five won't disappoint action junkies.<br /><br />Fast Five reunites Dom Toretto (Vin Diesel) with cop-turned-racer Brian O'Connor (Paul Walker) in the favelas of Rio de Janeiro. Diesel reprises his role of Toretto, this time on the run from a high-octane federal law enforcement team led by Luke Hobbs, played by Dwayne Johnson.<br /><br />Complicating their situation further is Brazilian drug kingpin Hernan Reyes, portrayed by veteran actor Joaquim de Almeida of \\"Desperado\\" fame. The only way to dig themselves out of their hole is to pull off a final caper to the tune of $100 million, aided by a variety of former series characters.<br /><br />What makes the latest addition to the Fast & Furious franchise a success is the amount of adrenaline injected into the film. Fast Five is chock full of tense moments, fast cars and shootouts. Adding a bit of levity to an otherwise hardcore action flick are the duo of reggaeton artists Don Omar and Tego Calderon, who return to the series with comedic relief in tow. Tyrese Gibson, Ludacris, Jordana Brewster, Sung Kang, and Matt Schulze also reprise their roles to offer a sense of familiarity to viewers.<br /><br />Fast Five's musical score is a mix of high-energy tracks with greater variety than other soundtracks from the franchise. The film's score doesn't feature as much American rap as earlier films, though it makes up for it with the inclusion of urban Portuguese-language songs from Brazil. International music ranges from Rio's rap to Brazilian Funk, plus the infectious \\"Danza Kuduro\\" by Puerto Rican reggaetonero Dom Omar, who returns to the film as the pessimistic Rico. Fast Five is the third film of the franchise that composer Brian Tyler contributes to, with songs ranging from cinematic to industrial rock.<br /><br />There are two elements of the film that stand out. The first being the too-good-to-be-true clash between Dom and federal strike team leader Luke Hobbs. The two reaching their inevitable on-screen collision hits with the force of a scud missile soaked in testosterone.<br /><br />The other element is the final car chase of the film. Gone are the intricate CGI shots of the mechanical workings of the cars involved. But what Fast Five loses in computer imaging, it makes up for with hardcore driving. The ultimate chase scene in the movie is far from what you've seen in other heist flicks, and is sure to please even the pickiest of action junkies.<br /><br />That's not to say that Fast Five is Oscar-quality, of course. To truly enjoy this film, you have accept in advance that this isn't Shawshank Redemption. While much of the cast have experience in film and television, the majority serve up average acting at best. I'm a huge fan of Vin Diesel's movies (Pitch Black FTW), but he looks all of his 44 years in this film, and his acting ability hasn't improved much. While he and Paul Walker both are well-suited for action flicks, don't expect profound performances from either of them. Diesel is given more of an opportunity to flex his acting chops in Fast Five, with it's emphasis on relationships and heartbreak, but I honestly wasn't too moved.<br /><br />Dwayne \\"The Rock\\" Johnson carries the greatest screen presence of the entire cast, giving off an air of intensity that resonates throughout every scene. But that being said, he wasn't given an opportunity to show off any real range of emotions in the film.<br /><br />Despite Fast Five having it's fair share of action and suspense, the film does drag on a bit longer than necessary with it's runtime of two-plus hours. While the film's conclusion is fairly clear, it's also given an open-ending that paves the way for the franchise's sixth effort, and the possible return of a significant character from the series.<br /><br />Overall, Fast Five is simply a fun watch, a guilty pleasure if you're a fan of heist flicks or action movies in general. If you're a motor head, you might be a bit let down at the abandonment of the franchise's original formula, though the change still make for a welcome spin on the series. Definitely get the Steelbook Blu-Ray to own one of the better movies in the series.><br />Overall, Fast Five is simply a fun watch, a guilty pleasure if you're a fan of heist flicks or action movies in general. If you're a motor head, you might be a bit let down at the abandonment of the franchise's original formula, though the change still make for a welcome spin on the series. Definitely get the Steelbook Blu-Ray to own one of the better movies in the series.

I was pleasantly surprised at how great it was.  I had heard reviews of this concert at the time as being much less than great, that they were unsure of themselves, that they stumbled along for a while huddling together during the show until they got their hard rock groove on. But what I saw was a band that started great and got greater as they got more comfortable, Until at the end of this show they were once again the greatest rock-n-roll band ever. From the beginning they were tight and they only got tighter as the progressed. From the start they were clearly enjoying themselves and that only became more apparent as the concert progressed. One of the things that made LZ great was their musicianship, but what I believe made them greater than just collaborating musicians was their chemistry.<br /><br />The whole point of any need of a reunion is that John Bonham died and the band had to dissolve at that time, and I think the whole point of any reunion is Jason Bohnam, Johns child, and the bands grandchild, because without him there is no reunion concert, no chemistry. Clearly he had that chemistry with the surviving members. I was so struck at how they took so much easy effort to include him as part of the band. He sings backup on the very first song, and Robert introduces him as featured on a later song. All during the show Jimmy, Robert, and John can be seen looking to him and smiling. They seem so happy for him that its almost secondary how happy they are for themselves to be playing as a band again. Besides those images, my evidence is that Robert says they are doing this for Ahmet Ertegun and Jason.<br /><br />This doesnt mean Jason actually replaces his father; no one can do that. Jason is a terrific drummer, and I can imagine no one but him ever playing drums with all the other members of Led Zeppelin, but while he may be the most able replacement, he his still not his father. Bonzo had a certain something that cannot be replaced, and I kept thinking of what was missing for the first two thirds of the concert, but I finally realized that Jason brought his own particular style to his dads drumming on all those songs, and he was damn good at it!<br /><br />Oh yeah, Jimmy was awesome, some of the best live guitar hes ever done. And Roberts voice is better than ever. JPJ is a wonderful musician that is the invisible glue that makes the band work, though he doesnt supply the magic that Bonzo did. Anyway, my major point is that there is a four-way magic recreated for a brief time that is so very much worth watching. They bring freshness to the songs and expertise that cannot be found in any tribute band.

You play an organism and eat other little organisms in a very fluid manner and you can rise to certain levels within the game, or take your way to the depths of this \\"ocean\\"; everything is very soothing. I actually had already purchased Flow for my PSP way back when, but didn't know too much about ThatGameCompany at the time.<br /><br />Flower is really fun! I smiled a lot playing this game it was peaceful and I had fun tilting the controller to move where I was going. The soundtrack here is also quite well done, and is very fitting.<br /><br />Journey is the best of the bunch here. This isn't just a game...it's an EXPERIENCE. I first watched the behind the scenes documentary prior to playing to get ready first. I had tried the demo a few months back, but I didn't understand it fully at the time either, so I put it down.<br />But now, I was ready to start my journey. You can take as long as you like...I took a few hours to play through my journey. I want to leave everything spoiler free--plus, a lot of people have already covered it so nicely--so I'll tell you right now, that this is probably the best game I've ever played. It brings back the wonders of gaming like when zelda and pokemon were new. Not that I'm comparing it to those games, but the feeling of trying something new, groundbreaking and so unique.<br />You literally travel across the world and examine ancient glyphs. There's no talking and no narrative. Just you, the landscape, and the music. Sometimes you'll run into people starting their journey as well. It was so exciting when I found someone and I chirped rapidly so they could see me. They chirped back and we met. We started traveling together and went through a majority of traveling together. I really liked how ThatGameCompany integrated the online aspect into Journey. No voice chat, no webcam thing, no text chatting...you can only communicate by musical chirps which works surprisingly really well in this game. While you journey alongside each other, it's like you create this type of silent bond with another person. Whenever I got seperated from my companion, I chirped rapidly so they could find me or they chirped so I could find them. We waited for each other to follow or we showed each other different spots in the game to gather these glowing cloth things that expand your scarf (to make you fly/glide longer). We helped each other during our journey. That just made the game even more of an experience. Whether alone or with a companion, it's totally unique.<br /><br />All you're doing is exploring this wonderous landscape of a world and experiencing...simply...a Journey.<br /><br />Best game ever. I wish it would get GOTY, but this IS the GOTY edition, with everything you get with this.<br />I think ThatGameCompany is onto big things and will only keep getting better and better at what they do.<br />I'm so glad I got to experience something like this. One more thing I would to add is that people said they cried during the game. Well, I didn't quite cry, but I did experience a little tearing up at some of the landscapes...with an epic soundtrack who can't get a little emotional! :)<br /><br />Don't play the demo, just get this or buy Journey on the Playstation Network.<br /><br />Trust me...it's a journey to experience.

Anyhoo, for a single 15 song set, it's worth its money.  As a rock journalist once wrote, and I believe it was Katherine Turner, although I could be wrong, \\"There are three things you can count on in life:  death, taxes, and an AC/DC concert.\\"  I saw them in Little Rock sometime around 1991 or so.  Malcolm Young was on sabbatical and replaced by their cousin Steve Young on rhythm guitar.  He didn't miss a beat.  Chris Slade was the drummer, and while I agree Phil Rudd has a bit more of a natural feel, being the drummer for so long, I simply could not complain about Slade live or on this disc, which I think was made shortly after Malcolm returned.<br />  It's actually good sense to have some live AC/DC because it's truly their format.  \\"If You Want Blood You've Got It\\" remains their definitive live statement with Bon Scott, and the newest live CD \\"Live At The River Plate\\" features some latter day material.  For those wanting a set with less newer material, this CD is probably preferable.  The band excel at simple blues based rock and roll, they've never screwed around with the formula, and as a result are one of the world's most loved bands.  Even snotty critics who loved to pan them in their earlier years have all of a sudden decided AC/DC are a great band.  I don't understand what was not to like, but critics have always been high brow pissants, loathe to like anything the masses did, and ended up championing loser bands and talentless crap that never went anywhere, just to have their own warped sense of \\"their music\\".  It's the same mentality as an art critic who thinks utter bullshit like Mark Rothko, who painted a canvas basically one or two colors with the precision and artistic flair of a cow handed a brush and a pallette.  It was an intellectual bullshit ruse made to make us think we were stupid and missing the point.  Same with critics who panned some of rock and roll's greatest music.<br />  Of course, seeing AC/DC and hearing them live is being on two different planets.  The between song banter is edited out, and we don't get to see Angus running amok, throwing himself into a seeming fit and still not missing a single note on his SG.  The power is there, though, and the mix allows Malcolm to be prominent on the left side of the mix with Angus on the other.  This highlights the interplay between the two brothers and shows how tight they are.  Highlights are the \\"Back in Black\\" cuts, \\"Shoot To Thrill\\" especially.  Brian Johnson doesn't sound like Bon Scott but his familiar growl works fine on old numbers like \\"Whole Lotta Rosie\\" and \\"TNT\\".<br />  All in all, it's a rocking set, although I would have liked to see something included from \\"Powerage\\", like the mighty \\"Down Payment Blues\\".  \\"Powerage\\" was the greatest Bon Scott era album, and deserved a cut on this album, hence the subtracting of one star.  Other than that, it's a great album at a good price.were stupid and missing the point.
